Go to the next screen.
Continue
Go to the previous screen.
Back
Quick Race allows you to run a race on any track. You have the option to select a truck from the quick race list or load a truck from your personal garage.
Quick Race
Versus allows you to play head to head against another local player.
Versus
Time Attack allows you to race for the fastest time on any track. You have the choice of running the Time Attack without a ghost racer, with your ghost racer, or with another player's ghost racer. A player's ghost racer is a fast lap replay with a translucent vehicle that cannot be collided with.
Time Attack
Career allows you to work through a career in a truck. You start by buying a stock vehicle. You can compete in a series of races to earn money. The money allows you to purchase off-road performance parts for your vehicle. The object of career is to create the fastest off-road racing vehicle possible.
Career
Network allows you to race other players anywhere in the world. You can play using one or two-player mode. Two player mode allows for split screen racing. To use the online mode, you need an Internet connection. Once you are connected, you are able to chat with other players and participate in races. Four players are allowed in a Dreamcast Network race.
Network
Replay allows you to watch a previously recorded replay. The replay mode functions like a VCR allowing play, fast forward, reverse play, slow motion, and related functionality. You can adjust the camera angles, change the selected vehicle, and freeze the action at any point.
Replay
Rankings allows you to view your best statistics on each track.
Rankings
Options allows you to setup the game according to your preferences. You can adjust controls, game play, and sound settings.
Options
The Credits section contains a list of all the people that worked on 4x4 Evolution.
Credits
Had enough racing?
Exit
One Player
Two Players
The available tire types are shallow cut, medium cut, deep cut, and studded. Each tire type is designed to provide optimum traction on certain surfaces. The shallow cut tire has no tread pattern and is designed for pavement only. The medium cut tire has a tread pattern designed for dirt and gravel roads. The deep cut tire has very aggressive tread pattern and is designed for mud, and sandy terrain. The studded tire has a tread pattern along with metal studs. The studded tire is designed for snow and ice roads.
Tire Type
The two available transmission types are automatic and manual. The automatic transmission performs shifting for you. The manual transmission requires you to do all up and down shifting. The manual transmission allows you to shift exactly when you want to where the automatic transmission only up or down shifts and preset rpm's. You may find that the automatic transmission is a little slow because it does not downshift very early.
Transmission
In order to enable the suspension setting your vehicle must be equipped with race springs/dampers. If your vehicle did not come equipped with race springs/dampers you can purchase them in career. The suspension settings allow you to adjust the relative stiffness of the spring/damper combination. A soft setting allows your vehicle to smoothly ride over bumps and rough terrain. A stiff setting makes your vehicle bounce over bumps and rough terrain. A soft setting makes your vehicle less responsive to steering input. A stiff setting makes your vehicle more responsive to steering input. A soft setting keeps your tires on the ground a lot for better acceleration. A stiff setting makes your car bounce more which may hurt acceleration on a bumpy circuit.
Suspension
In order to enable the axle ratio setting your vehicle must be equipped with a racing gear box or a ring and pinion gear set. If your vehicle did not come equipped with a racing gear box or a ring and pinion gear set you can purchase one in career. The axle ratio setting allows you to adjust the final drive of your vehicle. By adjusting the slider to the left your vehicle has greater acceleration but less top speed. Greater acceleration is useful on tracks that have lots of tight and twisty corners and no straights. If you adjust the slider to the right your vehicle has greater top speed potential but slower acceleration. Greater top speed potential is useful on tracks that have very fast corners and long straights.
Axle Ratio
In order to enable the brake balance setting your vehicle must be equipped with a brake proportioning valve. If your vehicle did not come equipped with a brake proportioning valve you can purchase one in career. The Brake Balance setting allows you to adjust how the vehicle behaves under braking. If the slider is adjusted towards the front (left side) the front brakes receive more power than the rear. More front braking causes your vehicle to be very stable under braking but very difficult to turn while braking. If the slider is adjusted towards the rear (right side) the rear brakes receive more power than the front. More rear braking causes your vehicle to be very unstable under braking but very easy to turn while braking.
Brake Balance
In order to enable the torque split setting your vehicle must be equipped with a racing transfer case. If your vehicle did not come equipped with a racing transfer case you can purchase one in career. The torque split setting allows you to adjust how power is distributed between the front and rear tires of your vehicle while in 4WD mode. If the slider is adjusted towards the front (left side) then the front tires receive more torque than the rear. More torque on the front tires helps steer the vehicle through the corners but can also cause your vehicle to understeer. The front tires spin easier than the rear if they have more torque. If the slider is adjusted to the rear (right side) then the rear tires receive more torque than the front. More torque on the rear tires helps the vehicle accelerate quicker. Too much torque on the rear can cause the rear tires to spin easily.
Torque Split
The handling balance slider allows you to adjust how the vehicle is balanced while cornering. If the slider is adjusted towards understeer (left side) the vehicle is easier to control but difficult to turn. If the slider is adjusted towards oversteer (right side) the vehicle is more difficult to control but turns very quickly. You want to run as much oversteer as you can handle with having the vehicle get sideways too much. If you are having problems controlling the vehicle you need to run less oversteer or more understeer.
Handling Balance

Vehicle Selection
Vehicle Settings
Go Race
Class 1 is composed of completely stock vehicles as they come off the showroom floor. Suspension travel and tire size may not be as great as the Class 2 and 3 vehicles but the stock power makes the Class 1 vehicles easy to drive.
Class 1 Vehicle (Rookie)
Class 2 is composed of vehicles that have been lightly modified for off-road racing. These modifications include improved wheel travel as well as larger tires to clear rocks and other obstacles. To improve performance in a straight line, power is slightly increased.
Class 2 Vehicle (Intermediate)
Class 3 is composed of vehicles that have been specifically modified for off-road racing. Wheel travel is increased substantially to improve handling over rough terrain. Tire size is increased to help clear obstacles. Power is increased to get down the straights quicker. The drivetrain is improved to help get the power to the road better.
Class 3 Vehicle (Professional)
A career vehicle is a vehicle that you have previously purchased and modified in career.
Career Vehicle
A custom vehicle is a vehicle that did not ship with the game - it was created by a user. Since the user can set any of the vehicle's variables, custom vehicles can have a wide range of performance and may not drive well in all situations. Use custom vehicles at your own risk.
Custom Vehicle

Color Selection
View Available Parts
Appearance items upgrade the exterior of your vehicle, making it look better. Some appearance items may have a slight effect on the vehicles aerodynamics and weight.
The brake section contains parts that you can purchase to improve the stopping performance of your vehicle.
The chassis section contains parts that you can purchase to improve the chassis of your vehicle. Typical improvements involve weight reduction and the stiffening of the chassis to improve handling.
The drivetrain section contains parts to improve the traction of your vehicle and the top speed or acceleration.
The electronics section contains electronic parts that you can purchase to improve the engine performance of your vehicle. Typical improvements include ignition systems and custom ECUs for fuel injection.
The engine section contains mechanical parts that you can purchase to improve the engine performance of your vehicle. Typical modifications include exhaust, ported cylinder heads, cold air intakes, etc.
The lights section contains parts to improve the lighting on your vehicle.
The suspension section contains parts to improve the handling, ground clearance, and suspension travel of your vehicle.
The tire section contains parts to improve the traction and ground clearance of your vehicle.
Starting a new hot lap allows you to create a new ghost lap on a track. You have the option of running with a ghost vehicle of your best lap during the session or without one. You can run up to 20 laps in your attempt to create a new ghost lap.
Start a new hot lap
Racing against an existing hot lap allows you to race against an existing ghost lap that you or someone else created. After selecting the file you want loaded the game loads the track and you can try to beat that ghost lap. You can run up to 20 laps in your attempt to beat the ghost lap.
Race against an existing hot lap
Viewing an existing hot lap allows you to watch an existing ghost lap.
View an existing hot lap

Series are competitions where the player competes in several races for an overall series championship. The player receives money based on their finishing position in each race.
Special Events are events that contain only a single race. The finishing position of the race determines how much money that you win.

You need to purchase a vehicle before you can race.
A series is a group of races where participants split a purse based upon finishing position. The money received after finishing a race can be used to purchase upgrades for your vehicle or to purchase a new vehicle.
Each series has specific criteria for participation. You can read the criteria for any given series by selecting the series. Each time you complete a race and upgrade your vehicle with the money you have won, new and more challenging series with higher total purses are available for you to race.
Once a series has been started, you must complete the races in order.  After completing a race, the next race becomes available. Each race in the series has a higher purse than the prior race. Once you complete a series, you can start that series over even though it is marked as completed.
A special event is a one-time race that may be specific to certain types or classes of vehicles. Each event is a single race with varying laps and conditions. All of the criteria of a special event must be met before you can participate. Special events can be raced as many times as you would like, and you are awarded a percentage of the total purse based upon finishing position. The money received after finishing a race can be used to purchase upgrades for your vehicle or to purchase a new vehicle.
